Ruling on Seeing the Outside of a Folded Garment
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-ru'ya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ru'ya for a folded garment, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Zufar, and apply the exception for material inner designs.

Core Idea
Seeing the outer side of a folded garment generally suffices, but the fatwa requires unfolding if inner details are valuable.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text addresses a specific scenario in sales: when a buyer purchases a folded garment after only seeing its outside, does the option of sight drop? The Hanafi school generally holds that seeing the outside suffices due to uniformity, but Imam Zufar disagrees and requires full unfolding. The relied-upon position today follows Zufar, yet an exception exists for garments with meaningful inner designs. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the contested ruling? The issue is whether seeing only the outside of a folded garment is sufficient to drop the buyer's option of sight (khiyar al-ru'ya).
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa and the majority hold that it suffices because the edges of a garment are similar; one part infers the rest. Minor variations are ignored.
The text says: 'because from seeing its edge one infers the rest, since the edges of a single garment do not differ except slightly, and that is not considered.'
3
Explain Zufar's objection
Zufar requires the garment to be unfolded and seen in its entirety, as the interior may differ in ways not apparent from the outside.
The text says: 'According to Zufar, it is necessary to unfold it and see all of it, and the fatwa is on his statement.'
4
Analyse the exception
Both sides agree that if the interior contains something intended for sight (e.g., a logo or design), seeing the outside does not drop the option. The buyer must see that part.
The text says: 'if there is something in the interior of the garment that is intended for sight, like the place of a logo, the face of a turban, etc., then in that case his option does not fall without unfolding according to all.'
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa is Zufar's position: the garment must be unfolded and seen entirely to drop the option, unless the interior has material designs (in which case even Zufar's requirement applies, but the option remains regardless).
The text explicitly states: 'al-fatwa 'ala qawlihi' (the fatwa is on his statement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظاهر الثوب مطويّاً. وظاهر الثوب: أي كفت رؤية ظاهر الثوب حال كونه مطوياً؛ لأنه يستدل برؤية طرف منه على الباقي؛ إذ لا تتفاوت أطراف الثوب الواحد إلا يسيرا وذا غير معتبر، قال الأقطع ومتى وجد داخل الثوب مختلفاً فهو عيب، ولا تعلق له بخيار الرؤية، وعند زفر: لابد من نشره ورؤية كله، والفتوى على قوله، وفي "النهر" "المبسوط" : : الجواب على ما قاله زفر وعند الجمهور: لا حاجة إلى النشر إذا لم يكن في طي الثوب ما يكون مقصوداً، فإن كان في باطن الثوب ما يقصد بالنظر كموضع العلم، ووجه العمامة ونحوه، فحينئذ لا يسقط خياره بدون النشر عند الكل.
And the outside of the folded garment (suffices). The outside of the garment: meaning that seeing the outside of the garment while it is folded suffices, because from seeing its edge one infers the rest, since the edges of a single garment do not differ except slightly, and that is not considered. Al-Aqta' said: When the inside of the garment is found to be different, it is a defect, and it is not related to the option of sight. According to Zufar, it is necessary to unfold it and see all of it, and the fatwa is on his statement. In 'al-Nahr' and 'al-Mabsut', the answer is on what Zufar said. According to the majority, there is no need for unfolding if there is nothing in the fold that is intended. If there is something in the interior of the garment that is intended for sight, like the place of a logo, the face of a turban, etc., then in that case his option does not fall without unfolding according to all.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on khiyar al-ru'ya (option of sight) when a person buys a folded garment after only seeing its outer side. The Hanafi position, as derived from the text, is that seeing the outside suffices because all parts of a garment are similar; minor variations are ignored. Zufar, a prominent Hanafi disciple, disagrees and requires unfolding and seeing the entire garment. The fatwa (operative ruling) is on Zufar's view. However, an exception exists: if the inner part has something specifically valued (like a logo or design on the turban), then the buyer retains the option until he sees that part. This shows a nuanced approach: the general rule is sufficiency of outer sight, but an exception is made when inner details are material. The passage provides the legal reasoning (ta'lil) and the ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): The right of the buyer to rescind a sale after seeing the item if it does not match expectations.
ظاهر الثوب (zahir al-thawb): The outer side or surface of a garment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (fatwa) view regarding seeing a folded garment?
A) Seeing outside suffices unconditionally
B) Must unfold and see all
C) Depends on whether inner part has designs
D) Buyer must rely on description

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa requires unfolding a folded garment to drop the option of sight, but an exception exists when inner designs are material, where all agree the option remains.

Ruling on Seeing the Courtyard of a House
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on whether seeing courtyard suffices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether seeing the courtyard suffices for khiyar al-ru'ya and apply the mufta bihi view considering custom.

Core Idea
The sufficiency of courtyard sight depends on custom; Zufar's view requiring interior sight is preferred.

When you buy a house without seeing it, Islamic law grants you the option of sight upon viewing. But what counts as sufficient sight? Does glancing at the courtyard drop your right to return the house if you dislike the interior? This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a classic Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Zufar, and shows how custom ('urf) can reshape a legal ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify what the matn initially states: seeing the courtyard (dakhil al-dar) suffices to drop the option, as if the entire house were seen.
The text says 'إذا رأى صحن الدار يسقط خياره'.
2
Identify the opponent (Zufar) and his view
Zufar disagrees: seeing the interior rooms is necessary. His view is labeled 'al-asahh' (the soundest).
زفر: لا بد من رؤية داخل البيوت وهو الأصح
3
Analyze Zufar's proof
Zufar argues that interior rooms have different benefits (manafi'), so they are not like uniform commodities where seeing a sample suffices. The house is not min dhawat al-amthal (items with equivalents).
لأن منافع البيوت الداخلة تختلف... لأنه ليس من ذوات الأمثال
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The original ruling was based on Kufan custom ('adah) where houses were built identically. Today, houses differ, so the ruling may not apply.
ما ذكره الشيخ مبني على عادة أهل الكوفة... وأما اليوم فبخلافه
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the role of custom
The later preference (mufta bihi) is Zufar's view, but if local custom makes houses uniform, Abu Hanifa's view could be relevant. The student must evaluate the custom.
Tarjih: Zufar is preferred; custom can shift the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وداخل الدار: التعسر رؤية الجميع، وكفي، ونظر ضرع شاة وذوق مطعوم وشم مشموم. أي كفت رؤية داخل الدار فإنها كرؤية كلها، وفي عامة الروايات: إذا رأى صحن الدار يسقط خياره وإن لم ير بيوتها، وكذا إذا رأى خارج الدار أو أشجار البستان من خارج. وقال زفر: لا بد من رؤية داخل البيوت وهو الأصح؛ لأن منافع البيوت الداخلة تختلف فلابد من رؤية ذلك كله؛ لأنه ليس من ذوات الأمثال، فلا يعرف كله برؤية بعضه، وما ذكره الشيخ مبني على عادة أهل الكوفة، فإن في ذلك الزمان دورهم كانت على تقطيع واحد، وأما اليوم فبخلافه فلا يكتفى برؤية داخل بالدار.
And the inside of the house (suffices). It is difficult to see all of it, and it suffices. And seeing the udder of a sheep, tasting food, smelling a scent (suffices). Meaning that seeing the inside of the house suffices and is like seeing it all. In most transmissions: if he sees the courtyard of the house, his option falls even if he did not see its rooms. Similarly, if he sees the outside of the house or the trees of the garden from outside. Zufar said: it is necessary to see the inside of the rooms, and this is the soundest because the benefits of the inner rooms differ, so it is necessary to see all of that because it is not like items that have equivalents, so all cannot be known by seeing some. What the shaykh mentioned is based on the custom of the people of Kufa, since in that time their houses were of a single pattern. But today it is different, so seeing the inside of the house is not sufficient.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage deals with khiyar al-ru'ya when the purchased property is a house. The Hanafi position as per the matn is that seeing the courtyard (dakhil al-dar) suffices to drop the option. Zufar again opposes, requiring sight of every interior room because their utilities differ. The text notes that the original ruling was based on Kufan custom where houses were uniform, but in other places it may not apply. This again shows the role of custom ('urf) in modifying legal rulings. The passage also mentions analogous cases: seeing a sheep's udder, tasting food, smelling a scent suffice for their respective products.

Key Terms
داخل الدار (dakhil al-dar): The interior or courtyard of a house, not necessarily the private rooms.
عادة (ada): Custom; used here to justify the ruling based on Kufan building patterns.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Zufar require seeing the interior rooms?
A) Because the Quran commands it
B) Because interior rooms have different benefits
C) Because it is the Sunnah
D) Because the buyer requested it

Key Takeaway
When a house is not uniform, seeing the courtyard alone does not drop the option of sight; Zufar's view requiring interior sight is the soundest.

Distinguishing Agent and Messenger in Khiyar al-Ru'ya
Ruling on khiyar al-ru'ya with agent vs messenger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ru'ya when an agent or messenger receives the sold item, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Agent's sight drops the option; messenger's does not—authority to litigate is the decisive factor.

When a buyer purchases an unseen item, the option of sight allows return upon seeing it. But what if someone else receives it on his behalf? Does their sight count? The Hanafi school distinguishes between an agent (wakil) who can litigate and a mere messenger (rasul) who cannot. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differed with Abu Hanifa on this point. Let's unpack the ruling and the debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the receipt of a sold item by another person on behalf of the buyer. The ruling is that if it is an agent (wakil), his sight is like the buyer's own and drops the option; if it is a messenger (rasul), his sight does not drop the option.
The key is the authority to litigate.
2
Distinguish wakil and rasul based on authority
The wakil has the right to litigate if the seller refuses delivery; the rasul does not. This is the 'illa (effective cause) for the difference in ruling.
Litigation authority indicates the agent acts as the principal's representative in a fuller sense.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds the distinction above. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say both agent and messenger are the same: their sight drops the option. This is also a narration from Abu Hanifa and the view of the other three imams.
The Sahibayn treat any representative's sight as sufficient.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) gives Abu Hanifa's view as the primary ruling. In fatwa, this is the relied-upon position, though the Sahibayn's view is also known.
The text explicitly says 'la nazara rasulihi', indicating messenger's sight does not count.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونظرُ وكيله بالقبض كنظره، لا نظر رسوله. صورته: أن يقول المشتري لغيره كن وكيلاً عني بقبض المبيع. وصورة الرسول: أن يقول: كن رسولاً عني بقبضه. والفرق بين الوكيل والرسول أن الوكيل يملك الخصومة إذا امتنع البائع عن التسليم. والرسول لا يملك، فلو طعاماً لم يره، فوكل رجلاً بالقبض، فقبضه الوكيل بعد ما رآه فليس للمشتري أن يرده إلا من عيب، والمعتبر رؤية التي مع القبض دون التي بعده، والرؤية قبل التوكيل لا أثر بها، فلا يسقط بها الخيار، وإن أرسل رسولاً بقبضه، فقبضه الرسول بعد ما رآه فللمشتري أن يرده، وقالا الوكيل والرسول سواء، وللمشتري أن يرده إذا رآه، وهو رواية عنه، وبه قالت الثلاثة، وهذا الخلاف في الوكيل بالقبض، فأما الوكيل بالشراء فرؤيته تسقط الخيار إجماعاً.
And the sight of his agent for receipt is like his own sight, not the sight of his messenger. Its image: that the purchaser says to another, 'Be a deputy for me in receiving the sold item.' The image of the messenger: that he says, 'Be a messenger for me in receiving it.' The difference between the agent and the messenger is that the agent possesses the right of litigation if the seller refuses delivery, while the messenger does not. So if someone buys food he has not seen, then appoints a man as agent for receipt, and the agent receives it after having seen it, the purchaser may not return it except for a defect. The sight considered is that which accompanies receipt, not after. Sight before appointment has no effect, so it does not drop the option. If he sends a messenger for receipt, and the messenger receives it after having seen it, the purchaser may return it. And the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the agent and messenger are the same, and the purchaser may return it when he sees it, and this is a narration from him (Abu Hanifa). And the three (imams) said this. This disagreement is regarding the agent for receipt. As for the agent for purchase, his sight drops the option by consensus.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage explains the nuanced difference between a wakil (agent) and a rasul (messenger) in khiyar al-ru'ya. An agent has broader authority including litigation, so his sight is considered like the principal's. A messenger is merely a conveyor, so his sight does not drop the principal's option. There is intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Hanifa distinguishes, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad treat them equally (the purchaser can still return upon seeing). The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's according to the text, but the two companions have their view. The ruling is specific to agents for receipt; for agents for purchase, all agree that their sight drops the option.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): An agent with the authority to act on behalf of the principal, including litigation.
رسول (rasul): A messenger who merely conveys without independent authority.
الخصومة (al-khusuma): The power to litigate or initiate legal proceedings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, what is the 'illa for the difference between an agent and a messenger in khiyar al-ru'ya?
A) The agent is paid; the messenger is not.
B) The agent can litigate; the messenger cannot.
C) The agent must be a relative; the messenger cannot.
D) The agent sees the item before the messenger.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the sight of a wakil (agent) for receipt drops the option of sight, but the sight of a rasul (messenger) does not, due to the agent's authority to litigate.

When Senses Beyond Sight Drop the Option of Sight
Ruling that khiyar al-ru'ya falls by touch, smell, taste before purchase, with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which khiyar al-ru'ya falls by touch, smell, or taste, and identify when description suffices for real estate and other items.

Core Idea
The option of sight falls not only by seeing but also by any sense that fully reveals the item before purchase.

When you buy an item unseen, Islamic law grants you the option to return it if you discover a defect. But what if you used another sense—touch, smell, taste—before buying? The Hanafi school expands the concept: any sensory inspection that adequately informs you about the item drops this option from the start. However, timing is critical: the inspection must occur before the contract, not after.

Guided Path
1
Locate the base ruling
Identify the core statement: the option falls (yasqut khiyaruhu) if the buyer uses touch (jass), smell (shamm), or taste (dhawq) on the sold item before purchase. For real estate, description (wasf) suffices.
This is the general rule from the matn.
2
Identify the timing condition
The commentator clarifies that this ruling applies only when the sensory inspection occurs before the purchase. If the inspection happens after the contract, the option remains and extends until something indicates satisfaction.
The key distinction: pre-purchase vs post-purchase inspection.
3
Analyze sufficiency of the sense
The sense used must be sufficient for that type of item. For example, touch suffices for garments, smell for perfumes, taste for foods. If more information is needed (e.g., length and width for a garment), touch alone is not enough—additional description is required.
Sufficiency is determined by what is normally known by that sense.
4
Apply the exception for real estate and similar items
For items like real estate, trees, and slaves, which cannot be known by touch, smell, or taste, the option falls by a complete description (wasf bī aghall mā yumkin).
This is because there is no other way to know them before buying.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسقط خياره إذا اشترى بحس المبيع وشمه وذوقه، وفي العقار بوصفه. وسقط خياره إلخ : محمول على ما إذا وجد الجس ونحوه منه قبل الشراء، أما إذا اشترى قبل الجس لا يسقط خياره بالجس، بل يثبت باتفاق الروايات ويمتد إلى أن يوجد منه ما يدل على الرضاء من قول أو فعل على الصحيح. ثم الاكتفاء بالجس مقيد بما يدرك به، ولا يحتاج إلى غيره، فإن احتيج إلى غير بالجس لابد منه كإن اشترى ثوباً لابد من صفة طوله وعرضه ورقعته مع الجس، وفي الحنطة لابد من والصفة. إذا اشترى: إذا كان المبيع مما يعرف بالجس إذا وجد الجس منه قبل الشراء. وشمه: أي ويسقط خياره إذا اشترى مبيعا بشم المبيع إن كان المبيع مما يعرف بالشم. وذوقه: أي وكذا إذا اشترى مطعوماً يعرف بالذوق. وفي العقار إلخ والشجر والعبد، وكل ما لا يعرف بالجس والشم والذوق يسقط خياره بوصف العقار؛ لأنه لا سبيل إلى معرفته إلا بالوصف بأبلغ ما يمكن.
And his option falls if he buys by feeling the sold item, smelling it, and tasting it. And for real estate, by its description. The phrase 'his option falls etc.' is carried upon when he performed touch etc. before the purchase. As for if he bought before touching, his option does not fall by touching, but rather it is established by agreement of the transmissions and extends until something indicating satisfaction from his words or action, according to the sound opinion. Then sufficiency by touch is restricted to what can be perceived by it and does not need other; if more than touch is needed, it is necessary, e.g., if he buys a garment, description of its length, width, and patch is needed along with touch. And for wheat, description is needed. 'If he buys': if the sold item is known by touch, if he performed touch before purchase. 'And smelling it': his option falls if he buys by smelling it if the sold item is known by smell. 'And tasting it': similarly if he buys food known by taste. And for real estate etc., trees and slave, and everything not known by touch, smell, or taste, his option falls by description of the real estate because there is no way to know it except by description in the most complete manner possible.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage explains that khiyar al-ru'ya does not only fall by seeing; it can also fall by using other senses appropriate to the item. For example, touching (jass) suffices for items like cloth, smelling for perfumes, tasting for foods. However, this only applies if the sense is used before the purchase. If the purchase was made without any sensory inspection, the option remains. For real estate, trees, and slaves, which cannot be known by touch/smell/taste, description suffices to drop the option. The commentary also notes that the sense must be sufficient; if more is needed (e.g., for a garment, length and width must be described with touch), it must be provided.

Key Terms
جس (jass): Touching or feeling the item with the hand to ascertain its quality.
شم (shamm): Smelling the item.
ذوق (dhawq): Tasting the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does touching (jass) drop the option of sight?
A) Anytime
B) Only if done before purchase
C) Only if done after purchase
D) Never

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, khiyar al-ru'ya falls not only by sight but also by any sense that adequately reveals the item, provided the inspection occurs before the contract.

Returning Both Garments When Only One Seen in a Single Sale
Ruling on khiyar when one of two garments in a single sale is seen

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on returning two garments purchased in a single contract when only one was seen, explain why returning one alone is prohibited, and distinguish this from khiyar al-'ayb.

Core Idea
If you buy two together after seeing only one, you must return both or keep both — splitting the contract is banned.

When you buy multiple items in a single sale (صفقة واحدة), your right to return is governed by special rules. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains what happens if you see only one garment before purchase. The key principle is the prohibition of splitting the contract (تفريق الصفقة). Understanding this ruling deepens your grasp of khiyar al-ru'ya and its limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Transaction Type
Recognize that the two garments were bought in a single contract (safqah wahidah) after seeing only one. This triggers the specific ruling.
The prohibition of splitting the contract applies only when items are sold as one unit.
2
State the Ruling on Return
Upon seeing the unseen garment, the buyer may return both garments, but not just one. The option (khiyar) remains for the unseen item, but returning one alone would split the contract.
The buyer's khiyar al-ru'ya attaches to the unseen item, but the contract prohibits partial return.
3
Identify the Proof
The ruling is based on the prohibition of splitting the contract (tafriq al-safqah). The buyer cannot keep one and return the other because that would cancel the contract in part.
This prohibition is established in hadith and Hanafi usul.
4
Contrast with Khiyar al-'Ayb
In khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect), after receipt the buyer can return only the defective item because the contract can be split in that context. This highlights that khiyar al-ru'ya is more restrictive.
Timing and type of option affect whether splitting is allowed.
5
Apply to Analogous Cases
If a defect is found before receipt, the same rule applies: cannot return one alone. If one garment is found to be owned by another, the buyer returns the remaining. This shows consistency in protecting a unified contract.
The principle applies broadly to prevent partial rescission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن رأى أحد الثوبين فاشتراهما، ثم رأى الآخر له ردّهما، ولا يورث كخيار الشرط. له ردهما: أي رد الثوبين إن شاء؛ لأن رؤية أحدهما لا تغني عن رؤية الآخر للتفاوت، فبقي خياره فيما لم يره وليس له أن يرده وحده؛ لنهيه عليها عن تفريق الصفقة، فيردهما جميعاً ضرورة. وكذا لو وجد بأحدهما عيبا قبل القبض ليس له أن يرده وحده، ولو استحق أحدهما رد الباقي؛ لأن الصفقة تمت فيما كان ملك البائع، ولو وجد العيب بعد القبض حيث لا يمتنع رد المعيب وحده؛ لأنه في خيار العيب يملك تفريق الصفقة بعد القبض، بخلاف خيار الرؤية.
And whoever sees one of two garments and buys both, then sees the other, he may return both. And it is not inherited like the option of condition. (Commentary: he may return both if he wishes because seeing one does not suffice for seeing the other due to difference, so his option remains for what he did not see. He may not return it alone because he is prohibited from splitting the contract, so he returns both out of necessity. Similarly, if he finds a defect in one before receipt, he may not return it alone. If one is found to be owned by another, he returns the remaining; because the contract was complete on what was the seller's property. If he finds a defect after receipt, where he can return the defective one alone, it is different because in option of defect, he can split the contract after receipt, unlike option of sight.)
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation where a person buys two garments as a single sale (صفقة واحدة) after seeing only one. The rule: he may return both, not just one, because seeing one doesn't inform about the other. He cannot keep one and return the other as that would split the contract (تفريق الصفقة) which is prohibited. The passage distinguishes this from khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect), where after receipt, he can return only the defective item and keep the good one. This shows that khiyar al-ru'ya is more restrictive regarding splitting the contract.

Key Terms
صفقة واحدة (safqah wahidah): A single transaction/contract involving multiple items.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): Option of defect; after receipt, buyer can return the defective item alone.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): Option of sight; buyer who buys an unseen item has the right to return it upon seeing it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone buys two garments after seeing only one, and then finds a defect in one garment before receipt?
A) He may return only the defective garment
B) He must return both garments
C) He may return either garment
D) He cannot return any garment

Key Takeaway
In a single contract for multiple items, khiyar al-ru'ya does not allow returning only the unseen item; the buyer must return all or none due to the prohibition of splitting the contract.

The Option of Sight is Not Inherited
Ruling that khiyar al-ru'ya does not pass to heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that khiyar al-ru'ya is not inherited and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The option of sight is personal to the contracting party and does not pass to heirs upon death.

When a buyer purchases an unseen item, he has the right to rescind upon seeing it. But what happens if he dies before seeing it? This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on whether this right is inherited.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Khiyar al-ru'ya is not inherited; it lapses upon the death of the contracting party.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Al-Shafi'i (old opinion) holds that the heir stands in the place of the deceased regarding the option.
This is the 'old' Shafi'i opinion; his new opinion is that selling what one has not seen is invalid.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The option was established by textual evidence only for the contracting party; the heir is not a contracting party, so the text does not extend to him.
Hanafi proof: 'the option was established for the contracting party by text.'
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Khiyar is a personal attribute (wasf), not a property right; inheritance applies to property, not personal attributes.
Analogy to khiyar al-shart, which also is not inherited.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi, if the buyer dies before sight, the option ends and the sale is binding. Under Shafi'i (old), heirs can still exercise the option.
Practical difference affects whether heirs can cancel the sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يورث أي إذا مات العاقد قبل الرؤية تبطل خياره ولا ينتقل إلى ورثته. وقال الشافعي: يقوم وارثه مقامه في التصرف بحكم الخيار. ولنا أن الخيار إنما ثبت للعاقد بالنص، والوارث ليس بعاقد فلا يثبت له. وما سبق من قول الشافعي من أن شراء ما لم يره يره لا يجوز كان هو قوله الجديد وما ذكر ههنا هو قوله القديم. كخيار الشرط: أي كما لا يورث خيار الشرط؛ لأن الخيار وصف فلا يجري فيه الإرث.
And it is not inherited: i.e., if the contracting party dies before sight, his option becomes void and does not transfer to his heirs. Al-Shafi'i said: his heir stands in his place in disposing of the item by virtue of the option. Our (Hanafi) proof: the option was established for the contracting party by text; the heir is not a contracting party, so it is not established for him. What preceded from al-Shafi'i that buying what one has not seen is not valid was his new opinion, and what is mentioned here is his old opinion. Like the option of condition: i.e., just as the option of condition is not inherited, because the option is an attribute (wasf) and thus inheritance does not run in it.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage establishes that khiyar al-ru'ya does not pass to the heirs of the buyer or seller upon death. The Hanafi position is that the option is personal to the contracting parties. Imām al-Shafi'ī differed, holding that heirs step into the shoes of the deceased regarding the option. The Hanafi proof is that the option was given by the Law (Sharī'a) only to the 'āqid (contracting party); the heir is not an 'āqid, so it does not transfer. The text also notes that this is analogous to khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) which is also not inherited because khayār is a 'wasf' (attribute) that does not run in inheritance.

Key Terms
يورث (yūrath): Passes by inheritance to heirs.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Option of stipulation; an agreed period to rescind or confirm the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is khiyar al-ru'ya not inherited according to the Hanafis?
A) Because death invalidates all contracts
B) Because the option is personal to the contracting party
C) Because the heirs can sue
D) Because the item becomes ownerless

Key Takeaway
The option of sight is a personal right that lapses upon death and does not pass to heirs, distinguishing it from property rights.

Forfeiture of Option of Sight Through Sensory Examination
Ruling on when the option of sight is lost after sensory examination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah) is forfeited in Hanafi fiqh and identify the intra-madhhab differences regarding blind buyers.

Core Idea
Touching, smelling, or tasting before purchase forfeits the option; for the blind, a detailed description suffices.

This passage clarifies when a buyer loses the right to rescind a contract due to not seeing the item. The general rule is that any sensory examination before purchase — touch, smell, taste — forfeits the option, provided the item is known by that sense. For real estate and items beyond sensory reach, a description serves. The commentary explores nuances, especially for blind buyers, where multiple Hanafi positions exist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the forfeiting actions
From the main ruling, list the actions that cause the option to fall: touching, smelling, tasting, and description (for real estate). Note that these must occur before purchase.
The action must be appropriate for the item's nature.
2
Distinguish pre-purchase vs post-purchase examination
Understand that if the examination occurs after purchase, the option does not fall; it remains until the buyer indicates satisfaction explicitly.
This is a critical timing condition.
3
Examine the blind buyer's situation
Analyze the three Hanafi views: description alone (standard), placing the blind in a location (Abu Yusuf), or appointing an agent (Hasan). The Balkh view adds touching walls with description.
The text favors the agent method as closest to Abu Hanifa's position.
4
Apply the rule on permanence of forfeiture
Once the option falls, it does not return even if sight is regained. Similarly, if a sighted buyer becomes blind before seeing, the option converts to description.
Satisfaction, once indicated, finalizes the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسقط خياره إذا اشترى بحس المبيع وشمه وذوقه، وفي العقار بوصفه، ومن رأى أي و كفت رؤية عنه الأعمى قبل الشراء. وسقط خياره إلخ : محمول على ما إذا وجد الجس ونحوه منه قبل الشراء، أما إذا اشترى قبل الجس لا يسقط خياره بالجس، بل يثبت باتفاق الروايات ويمتد إلى أن يوجد منه ما يدل على الرضاء من قول أو فعل على الصحيح [ رمز الحقائق: ۱۹/۲] ثم الاكتفاء بالجس مقيد بما يدرك به، ولا يحتاج إلى غيره، فإن احتيج إلى غير بالجس لابد منه كإن اشترى ثوباً لابد من صفة طوله وعرضه ورقعته مع الجس، وفي الحنطة لابد من والصفة. (عيني، فتح) إذا اشترى: إذا كان المبيع مما يعرف بالجس إذا وجد الجس منه قبل الشراء. (عيني) وشمه: أي ويسقط خياره إذا اشترى مبيعا بشم المبيع إن كان المبيع مما يعرف بالشم. (عيني) وذوقه: أي وكذا إذا اشترى مطعوماً يعرف بالذوق. (عيني) وفي العقار إلخ والشجر والعبد، وكل ما لا يعرف بالجس والشم والذوق يسقط خياره بوصف العقار؛ لأنه لا سبيل إلى معرفته إلا بالوصف بأبلغ ما يمكن. (ط، عيني)] لأن الوصف يقام مقام الرؤية في حق البصير كما في السلم حتى لا يكون له خيار الرؤية بعد ما وصف له، فكذا في حقه فيسقط خياره بعد وصف العقار، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يشترط ذلك أن يوقف الأعمى في مكان مع لو كان بصيراً لرآه . منه؛ لأن المصير إلى التشبيه عند تعذر الحقيقة واجب كالمحرم إذا أراد التحلل وقد قرع رأسه يلزم إجرار الموسى تشبيهاً بالمحلقين، وكذا الأخرس يلزمه تحريك الشفتين عند القراءة. وقال الحسن: يوكل وكيلاً بقبضه له، والوكيل يراه وهو أشبه بقول أبي حنيفة؛ لأن نظر الوكيل كنظره عنده، وقال بعض أئمة بلخ: يسقط خياره بمس الحيطان والأشجار مع الوصف، وإن وجد البصر بعد الوصف أو بعد ما وجد منه ما يدل على الرضاء فلا خيار له؛ لأن العقد تم بوجود ما دل على الرضاء وسقط الخيار، فلا يعود ولو اشترى البصير ثم عمي قبل الرؤية انتقل الخيار إلى الوصف؛ لوجود العجز قبل العلم به رمز الحقائق: ١٩/٢] (كفاية)
And his option falls if he buys by touching the sold item, smelling it, and tasting it, and for real estate by its description, and one who saw... and that suffices as sight for the blind before purchase. The [commentary] says: This is carried on the case where touching and the like occur before purchase. But if he bought before touching, his option does not fall by touching; rather it is established by agreement of the narrations and extends until something indicating satisfaction from him appears, in word or deed, according to the correct view. Then reliance on touching is restricted to what can be perceived by it, and no need for other. If other is needed through touching, it is necessary, as if he bought a garment – the description of its length, width, and patch is needed along with touching, and for wheat, description is needed. (Ayni, Fath) 'When he buys': if the sold item is known by touching, if touching occurs before purchase. (Ayni) 'Smelling it': i.e., his option falls if he buys a sold item by smelling it, if the sold item is known by smell. (Ayni) 'Tasting it': i.e., likewise if he buys an edible known by taste. (Ayni) 'And for real estate etc.': and trees, and a slave, and everything not known by touching, smelling, tasting – his option falls by description of the real estate; because there is no way to know it except by description in the most complete manner possible. (T, Ayni) Because description takes the place of sight for the sighted as in salam, such that he has no option of sight after it is described to him, so likewise in his right, his option falls after description of the real estate. And from Abu Yusuf that it is conditioned that the blind man be placed in a location such that if he were sighted he would see it. Because resorting to analogy when the reality is impossible is obligatory, like the muhrim who wants to exit ihram and has shaved his head – it is necessary to pass the razor analogizing to those who shave, and likewise the mute must move his lips during recitation. And al-Hasan said: He appoints an agent to take delivery for him, and the agent sees it, which is more similar to the view of Abu Hanifa, because the agent's sight is like his sight according to him. And some scholars of Balkh said: His option falls by touching the walls and trees along with description. And if sight returns after description or after something indicating satisfaction appears from him, then he has no option; because the contract was completed by the existence of what indicates satisfaction and the option fell, so it does not return. And if a sighted person buys then becomes blind before sight, the option transfers to description; due to the existence of incapacity before knowledge of it. (Kifayah)
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on forfeiture of the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah) through sensory examination. The main ruling is that the option falls if the buyer, before purchase, touches, smells, or tastes the item (where applicable), or for real estate and items not perceptible by those senses, by description. The commentary elaborates: touching must occur before purchase; if after purchase, the option remains until explicit satisfaction. For items like cloth, description of length, width, and patches is needed alongside touching. For a blind person, description suffices, and Abu Yusuf requires placing the blind person in a location analogous to where a sighted person would see. Hasan ibn Ziyad suggests appointing an agent to see it, which aligns with Abu Hanifa's view. Some scholars of Balkh say touching walls and trees with description suffices. Once satisfaction is indicated (by word or deed), the option does not return even if sight is regained. If a sighted buyer becomes blind before seeing, the option transfers to description. These are all Hanafi positions, with some internal differences.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option of sight: the buyer's right to rescind a contract for an item not seen at contract, upon seeing it.
الجس (al-jass): Touching or feeling to determine the quality of an item.
الوصف (al-wasf): Description; verbal specification of an item's attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a blind buyer forfeit the option of sight for real estate?
A) Upon touching the walls
B) Upon receiving a detailed description
C) Upon appointing an agent
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ru'yah is forfeited by pre-purchase sensory examination or description; for the blind, description suffices and the option does not revive.

Returning Both Items When Unseen Item is Disliked in a Single Transaction
Ruling on khiyar al-ru'yah for multi-item safqah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ru'yah when two items are bought together, and distinguish it from khiyar al-'ayb regarding the splitting of a single transaction.

Core Idea
If you buy two items as one deal after seeing only one, you must return both if you dislike the unseen – you cannot split the sale.

In Hanafi fiqh, khiyar al-ru'yah gives the buyer the right to rescind after seeing an unseen item. But when two items are purchased together in a single transaction (safqah), returning only the unseen item would split the sale, which is prohibited. This lesson explains the rule and its exceptions, including the contrast with khiyar al-'ayb after possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The buyer sees one of two garments and purchases both as one lump sum (safqah). Later he sees the second and is unsatisfied. What are his options?
The transaction is a single deal, not two separate purchases.
2
Apply khiyar al-ru'yah
The buyer has the right to rescind regarding the unseen item because seeing one garment does not substitute for seeing the other due to potential differences.
Khiyar al-ru'yah is established for items not seen at the time of contract.
3
Understand the prohibition of splitting the safqah
Returning only the unseen item would split the single transaction, which is prohibited. Therefore, the buyer must return both items together.
This rule is based on the principle that a single sale should not be fragmented.
4
Compare with khiyar al-'ayb after possession
If a defect is found after taking possession, the buyer may return only the defective item because khiyar al-'ayb allows splitting the safqah post-possession, unlike khiyar al-ru'yah.
The timing and nature of the option matter: khiyar al-'ayb is an exception to the general prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحد الثوبين فاشتراهما، ثم رأى الآخر له ردّهما ، ولا يورث كخيار الشرط، المبيعين أي الثوبين صفقة واحدة أي المشتري أي الثوب الآخر. له ردهما: أي رد الثوبين إن شاء؛ لأن رؤية أحدهما لا تغني عن رؤية الآخر للتفاوت، فبقي خياره فيما لم يره وليس له أن يرده وحده؛ لنهيه عليها عن تفريق الصفقة، فيردهما جميعاً ضرورة رمز الحقائق: ٢٠/٢] وكذا لو وجد بأحدهما عيبا قبل القبض ليس له أن يرده وحده، ولو استحق أحدهما رد الباقي؛ لأن الصفقة تمت فيما كان ملك البائع، ولو وجد العيب بعد القبض حيث لا يمتنع رد المعيب وحده؛ لأنه في خيار العيب يملك تفريق الصفقة بعد القبض، بخلاف خيار الرؤية. (عيني، فتح)
One of the two garments, so he bought both, then saw the other – he has the right to return both. The two sold items: i.e., the two garments as one lump sum, i.e., the buyer [saw] the other garment. He has the right to return both: i.e., to return the two garments if he wishes; because seeing one does not suffice for seeing the other due to variation, so his option remains for what he did not see, and he may not return it alone; because of the prohibition of splitting the lump sum, so he returns both by necessity. Similarly, if he finds a defect in one before taking possession, he may not return it alone. And if one is claimed by someone else, he returns the remaining; because the transaction was completed regarding what was the seller's property. And if he finds the defect after taking possession, then he is not prevented from returning the defective one alone; because in the option of defect, he has the right to split the lump sum after possession, unlike the option of sight. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where a buyer sees one of two items (e.g., two garments) and then purchases both as a single transaction. Upon seeing the second item, the buyer retains the option of sight for that unseen item. However, he cannot return only the unseen item because that would split the single sale; he must return both items together. The same applies if a defect is found in one before taking possession – return requires both. If one item is claimed by a third party (istihqaq), the buyer returns the remaining item. Importantly, after possession, if a defect is found, the buyer may return only the defective item under khiyar al-‘ayb, unlike khiyar al-ru’yah where the lump sum cannot be split after possession.

Key Terms
صفقة (safqah): A single transaction or lump sum sale; the two items are sold together as one deal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer sees one of two garments and buys both as a single transaction. Upon seeing the second, he dislikes it. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) He can return only the second garment.
B) He must return both garments.
C) He can keep both and demand a price reduction.
D) He has no option because he saw one.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, khiyar al-ru'yah for a multi-item safqah requires returning the entire lot; only after possession does khiyar al-'ayb permit splitting the sale.

Option of Sight Not Inherited: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling on inheritance of option of sight and analogy with option of condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ru'yah upon the contractor's death and explain the difference with the Shafi'i old view.

Core Idea
Options are personal legal descriptions, not inheritable property rights.

This passage addresses whether the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah) passes to heirs if the contractor dies before exercising it. The Hanafi school rules that it is extinguished, while Imam al-Shafi'i held a different view in his earlier position. Understanding this distinction reveals a key Hanafi principle: options are not property but personal rights tied to the specific contractor.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its reasoning
Identify that the option terminates with the contractor's death because it is established by text only for the contractor, and the heir is not the contractor.
The key phrase is 'al-nass' indicating the option is personal.
2
Identify the Shafi'i old view and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i (in his old view) held that the heir stands in the place of the deceased to exercise the option. Note that his new view made the sale of an unseen item impermissible.
The text distinguishes qadim (old) from jadid (new).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the option is a description (wasf), not a property right, and inheritance does not apply to descriptions.
This is based on the analogy with khiyar al-shart.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, Hanafi heirs cannot rescind the contract; Shafi'i (old view) heirs could. This difference affects contract enforcement after a party's death.
In the new Shafi'i view, the sale itself is invalid, so the issue is moot.
5
Apply the analogy with khiyar al-shart
Just as the option of condition is not inherited, the option of sight is also not inherited because both are descriptions (awsaf). This reinforces the Hanafi principle.
Analogy (qiyas) is used to extend the ruling from khiyar al-shart to khiyar al-ru'yah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يورث أي إذا مات العاقد قبل الرؤية تبطل خياره ولا ينتقل إلى ورثته وقال الشافعي: يقوم وارثه مقامه في التصرف بحكم الخيار ولنا أن الخيار إنما ثبت للعاقد بالنص، والوارث ليس بعاقد فلا يثبت له، وما سبق من قول الشافعي من ؟ أن شراء ما لم يره يره لا يجوز كان هو قوله الجديد وما ذكر ههنا هو قوله القديم. [تبيين الحقائق: ٣٣٢/٤] (عيني، فتح، زيلعي) كخيار الشرط: أي كما لا يورث خيار الشرط؛ لأن الخيار وصف فلا يجري فيه الإرث. (عيني)
And it is not inherited: i.e., if the contractor dies before sight, his option becomes void and does not transfer to his heirs. Imam al-Shafi'i said: His heir stands in his place in exercising the option. Our evidence is that the option is established for the contractor by text ( نص ), and the heir is not a contractor, so it is not established for him. What preceded from al-Shafi'i – that purchasing what he has not seen is not permissible – was his new view, and what is mentioned here is his old view. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 4/332) (Ayni, Fath, Zayla'i) Like the option of condition: i.e., just as the option of condition is not inherited, because the option is a [legal] description and inheritance does not apply to it. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah) is not inherited. If the contracting party dies before seeing the item, the option is extinguished and does not pass to heirs. The Hanafi position is contrasted with Imam al-Shafi'i, who in his old view held that the heir succeeds the deceased in exercising the option. The Hanafi proof is that the option is granted specifically to the contractor, and since the heir is not the contractor, it does not transfer. The passage also draws an analogy to khiyar al-shart (option of condition), which likewise is not inherited because options are legal descriptions (awsaf) that are not subject to inheritance. This is a distinct Hanafi ruling, and the Shafi'i position is noted to be different in his new view (where selling an unseen item is impermissible altogether).

Key Terms
النص (al-nass): The primary textual evidence (Quran or Sunnah) that establishes the option for the contractor.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option to rescind a sale after seeing an item that was purchased unseen.
وصف (wasf): A legal description or attribute that is not a property right; here, the option is considered a wasf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a buyer dies before exercising the option of sight, can his heirs return the item?
A) Yes, they stand in his place
B) No, the option is void
C) Only if they also did not see it
D) Only for khiyar al-shart

Key Takeaway
The option of sight is a personal right of the contractor that terminates upon death and is not transferable to heirs, just like the option of condition.

8 min
The Core Ruling of Khiyar al-Ru'yah and Its Conditions
Explains basic khiyar al-ru'yah ruling and conditions for khiyar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of khiyar al-ru'yah and identify the conditions under which the buyer has the option.

Core Idea
A buyer who saw an item before purchase can rescind only if the item changed; unchanged means no option.

This lesson explains the foundational principle of khiyar al-ru'yah: the buyer who has seen the item has an option if it changes, but not if it remains the same. We will also explore how intent and knowledge at the time of sight affect this right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being evaluated: buying an item after seeing it. The ruling is that the buyer has the option (khiyar) if the item has changed since sight; otherwise the contract is binding.
This is the core ruling from the matn.
2
Determine the khiyar cause
If the item changed from the description seen, the contract is based on an unknown description, so the buyer may rescind. If unchanged, knowledge is complete, and the sale is binding.
The reason is that the contract occurred on an unknown description if changed.
3
Check conditions of sight
For the option to be valid, the buyer must have seen the item intending to purchase and must know at the time of purchase that it is the same item seen.
If sight was without purchase intent or the buyer did not realize it was the same item, he still has the option because consent was incomplete.
4
Apply exceptions
When the buyer saw without purchase intent or was unaware of prior sight, he retains the option to rescind regardless of change, as if he never saw it.
This is due to lack of true satisfaction without knowledge of attributes.

باب خيار الرؤية

كتاب البيوع ومن اشترى ما رأى خير إن تغيّر، وإلا لا، وإن اختلفا في التغير، فالقول للبائع، المشتري لا يخير البائع والمشتري في التغير العدل وللمشتري لو في الرؤية، ولو اشترى عدلاً وباع منه ثوباً، أو وهب وسلّم ردّه بعيب، لا بخيار رؤية أو شرط.

اختلفا ما رأى قبل البيع قاصداً لشرائه عالماً وقت الشراء بأنه مرئية. (ط) عيني) خير إن تغير: أي من اشترى شيئاً رآه قبل الشراء فله الخيار إن تغير الشيء عن الصفة التي رآه عليها قبل ذلك؛ لأن العقد وقع على مجهول الوصف. وإلا لا أي وإن لم يتغير الشيء عن الصفة التي رآه عليها لا يخير؛ لأن العلم بالمبيع قد حصل بالرؤية الأولى، وقد رضي به ما دام على تلك الصفة [رمز الحقائق: ٢٠/٢]
:
وهذا إذا كان وقت الرؤية قاصدا لشرائه عالما بأنه مرئية، فلو رآه لا لقصد شراء ثم شراه فله الخيار، وكذا لو لم يعلم وقت الشراء أنه مرئية يتخير أيضاً لعدم الرضاء؛ لأن الرضاء بدون العلم بأوصافه لا يتصور، وتلك الرؤية لم تقع معلمة له بأوصاف المبيع فصار كأنه لم يره. (فتح، زيلعي) وإن اختلفا في التغير فقال المشتري قد تغير وقال البائع لم يتغير فالقول للبائع مع اليمين، وعلى المشتري البينة؛ لأن الأصل بقاء ما كان على ما كان فلا يصدق المشتري في دعوى التغير إلا ببينته، وسبب اللزوم وهو رؤيته السابقة قد ظهر، والظاهر شاهد للبائع، فكان القول قوله وهذا إذا كانت المدة قريبة يعلم أنه لا يتغير في مثل تلك المدة، فإن بعدت المدة بأن رأى أمة شابة ثم اشتراها بعد عشرين سنة، وزعم البائع أنها لم تتغير فالقول للمشتري، والمدة تختلف باختلاف الأشياء كتغير الأشجار في سنة، والدواب بما دونها؛ لقلة الرعي، وقالوا: البعيد: الشهر فما فوقه، والقريب ما دون الشهر، وقيل: الشهر في مثل الدابة والمملوك قريب. (فتح) وللمشتري لو في الرؤية: أي إذا اختلف البائع والمشتري في الرؤية بأن قال البائع رأيته قبل البيع، وقال المشتري: ما رأيته قبل العقد، فالقول للمشتري بيمينه؛ لأنه أمر حادث والمشتري ينكره، فيكون القول قوله مع يمينه. رمز الحقائق: ۲۰/۲] عدلا أي عدل ثياب من القماش و لم يره وقبضه (ط) وهب وسلم: ثم اطلع على عيب في الباقي فهو بالخيار أمسكه إن شاء أو رده. (ط) رده بعيب: أي إذا اشترى عدل ثياب، فقبضه وتصرف في ثوب واحد من البيع أو الهبة مع التسليم، ثم وجد الباقي معيباً رده بسبب العيب، وليس البيع والهبة قيداً؛ لأن اللبس كذلك، ولا يمكنه أن يرد الباقي بخيار الرؤية والشرط سواء كان قبل القبض أو بعده؛ لما فيه من تفريق الصفقة قبل التمام، وفي خيار العيب يملك التفريق بعد القبض، فإن عاد إليه بسبب هو فسخ محض كالرد بخيار الرؤية أو الشرط أو العيب بقضاء أو الرجوع في الهبة، فهو على خيار الرؤية؛ لارتفاع المانع من الرد، وهو تفريق الصفقة، وعن أبي يوسف أن الخيار لا يعود؛ لأن الساقط لا يعود كخيار الشرط. (عيني، فتح) أو شرط لأن الرد قد تعذر بإخراج البعض عن ملكه. (فتح)
Chapter of Option of Seeing. From the book of Sales: And whoever buys what he saw has the option if it has changed, otherwise not. And if they dispute about the change, the statement is of the seller. The buyer does not have the option. The seller and buyer regarding the change: the just? And for the buyer regarding the seeing: And if he bought a bundle and sold from it a garment, or gifted and delivered, he returns it due to defect, not due to option of seeing or stipulation. They differed: He saw before the sale intending to purchase, knowing at the time of purchase that it is visible. (T, Ayni) He has option if it changed: meaning whoever bought something he saw before the purchase has the option if the thing changed from the description he saw it upon before that; because the contract occurred on an unknown description. Otherwise no: meaning if the thing did not change from the description he saw it upon, he has no option; because knowledge of the sold item was obtained by the first sight, and he was satisfied with it as long as it remains on that description. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 20/2] This is when at the time of seeing he intended to purchase, knowing that it is visible; if he saw it not intending to purchase then bought it, he has the option; similarly if he did not know at the time of purchase that it was visible, he also has the option due to lack of satisfaction; because satisfaction without knowledge of its attributes is inconceivable, and that sight did not inform him of the attributes of the sold item, so it is as if he did not see it. (Fath, Zayla'i) And if they dispute about the change: the buyer says it changed, the seller says it did not change, the statement is of the seller with oath, and the buyer bears the burden of proof; because the original principle is that what remains remains as it was, so the buyer is not believed in claiming change without his evidence, and the cause of bindingness—his prior sight—has appeared, and the apparent is a witness for the seller, so the statement is his. This is when the period is short, known that it does not change in such a period; if the period is long, such as he saw a young female slave then bought her after twenty years, and the seller claims she did not change, the statement is of the buyer. The period varies according to things: change of trees in a year, and animals in less due to lack of grazing. They said: remote is a month and above, near is less than a month; it is said: a month for animals and slaves is near. (Fath) And for the buyer regarding the seeing: if the seller and buyer dispute about the seeing, the seller says he saw it before the sale, the buyer says he did not see it before the contract, the statement is of the buyer with his oath; because it is an incident thing and the buyer denies it, so the statement is his with his oath. Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 20/2] 'Adlan: meaning a bundle of cloth fabric, and he did not see it and took possession (T), and gifted and delivered: then he discovered a defect in the rest, he has the option to keep it if he wishes or return it. (T) He returns it due to defect: if he bought a bundle of cloth, took possession, and disposed of one garment by sale or gift with delivery, then found the rest defective, he returns it due to the defect. Sale and gift are not restrictions because wearing is similar. He cannot return the rest due to option of seeing or stipulation, whether before or after possession, because it involves splitting the transaction before completion. In option of defect, he has the right to split after possession. If it returns to him due to a cause that is pure rescission, like return due to option of seeing, stipulation, defect by judgment, or revocation of gift, then he is upon option of seeing because the obstacle to return is removed—the splitting of the transaction. From Abu Yusuf: the option does not return because what falls does not return like option of stipulation. (Ayni, Fath) Or stipulation because the return has become impossible by removing some from his ownership. (Fath)
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage from Bab Khiyar al-Ru'yah explains the buyer's option when he has seen the item before purchase. The core ruling: if the item has changed from the state in which it was seen, the buyer has the option to rescind; if unchanged, the sale is binding. The author clarifies that this applies only if the buyer saw the item with the intention to purchase and was aware at the time of purchase that it was the same item he had seen. If he saw it without purchase intent, or did not know it was previously seen, the option exists because true satisfaction requires knowledge of attributes. When buyer and seller disagree on whether the item changed, the seller's word is taken with oath if the period is short; if long (e.g., twenty years), the buyer's word is taken. The definition of 'short' and 'long' varies: generally, less than a month is short, a month or more is long, but for animals and slaves a month may be considered short. If they dispute whether the buyer saw it at all, the buyer's word is taken because he denies a claim of prior sight. A sub-issue: if someone buys a bundle of cloth, uses one piece by sale or gift, then finds a defect in the rest, he may return the rest due to the defect — not due to khiyar al-ru'yah or khiyar al-shart — because using part splits the transaction. However, if the used piece is returned (e.g., by court judgment or revocation), the option of seeing is restored according to Abu Hanifa, because the obstacle is removed. Abu Yusuf holds it does not return, analogizing to khiyar al-shart.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): An option granted to a buyer who has seen the item before purchase to rescind the contract if the item has changed since inspection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a buyer have the option of khiyar al-ru'yah?
A) When the item has not changed since inspection.
B) When the item has changed since inspection.
C) When the buyer did not see the item at all before purchase.
D) When the seller lied about the price.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ru'yah exists only when the item changes from what was seen; otherwise the sale is binding.

Disputes in Khiyar al-Ru'yah and the Bundle Sub-Issue
Explains dispute resolution and the bundle sub-issue in khiyar al-ru'yah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the burden of proof when buyer and seller dispute about change or prior sight, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the bundle sub-issue.

Core Idea
When the item's change is disputed, the seller's word is taken in short periods; for sight itself, the buyer's word is taken.

This lesson covers the procedural rules when parties disagree about the change or the fact of prior sight. It also examines a specific case: a bundle of cloth where part is used and then the rest is found defective, leading to a difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on whether the option of seeing returns.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute type
Determine whether the dispute is about the item's change or about the fact of prior sight. Rules differ.
For change, burden is on buyer; for sight, burden is on seller.
2
Apply burden rules for change dispute
If the period since sight is short, the seller's word is taken with oath; if long (e.g., a month or more for many items), the buyer's word is taken. The definition of short/long varies by item.
Example: trees change in a year, animals in less than a month.
3
Apply burden rules for sight dispute
When parties dispute whether the buyer saw the item before purchase, the buyer's word is taken with oath because he denies a claim of prior sight.
This is based on the principle that the claimant must prove.
4
Analyze the bundle case
A bundle of cloth (adl) bought unseen. Buyer uses one piece by sale or gift, then finds rest defective. He can return the rest due to defect, but not via khiyar al-ru'yah or khiyar al-shart because using part splits the contract.
In defect option, splitting is allowed after possession.
5
Explore the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
If the used piece is returned (by rescission, court judgment, etc.), Abu Hanifa holds that the option of seeing returns because the obstacle (splitting) is removed. Abu Yusuf holds it does not return, analogizing to khiyar al-shart.
The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.

Source Text

باب خيار الرؤية

كتاب البيوع ومن اشترى ما رأى خير إن تغيّر، وإلا لا، وإن اختلفا في التغير، فالقول للبائع، المشتري لا يخير البائع والمشتري في التغير العدل وللمشتري لو في الرؤية، ولو اشترى عدلاً وباع منه ثوباً، أو وهب وسلّم ردّه بعيب، لا بخيار رؤية أو شرط.

اختلفا ما رأى قبل البيع قاصداً لشرائه عالماً وقت الشراء بأنه مرئية. (ط) عيني) خير إن تغير: أي من اشترى شيئاً رآه قبل الشراء فله الخيار إن تغير الشيء عن الصفة التي رآه عليها قبل ذلك؛ لأن العقد وقع على مجهول الوصف. وإلا لا أي وإن لم يتغير الشيء عن الصفة التي رآه عليها لا يخير؛ لأن العلم بالمبيع قد حصل بالرؤية الأولى، وقد رضي به ما دام على تلك الصفة [رمز الحقائق: ٢٠/٢]
:
وهذا إذا كان وقت الرؤية قاصدا لشرائه عالما بأنه مرئية، فلو رآه لا لقصد شراء ثم شراه فله الخيار، وكذا لو لم يعلم وقت الشراء أنه مرئية يتخير أيضاً لعدم الرضاء؛ لأن الرضاء بدون العلم بأوصافه لا يتصور، وتلك الرؤية لم تقع معلمة له بأوصاف المبيع فصار كأنه لم يره. (فتح، زيلعي) وإن اختلفا في التغير فقال المشتري قد تغير وقال البائع لم يتغير فالقول للبائع مع اليمين، وعلى المشتري البينة؛ لأن الأصل بقاء ما كان على ما كان فلا يصدق المشتري في دعوى التغير إلا ببينته، وسبب اللزوم وهو رؤيته السابقة قد ظهر، والظاهر شاهد للبائع، فكان القول قوله وهذا إذا كانت المدة قريبة يعلم أنه لا يتغير في مثل تلك المدة، فإن بعدت المدة بأن رأى أمة شابة ثم اشتراها بعد عشرين سنة، وزعم البائع أنها لم تتغير فالقول للمشتري، والمدة تختلف باختلاف الأشياء كتغير الأشجار في سنة، والدواب بما دونها؛ لقلة الرعي، وقالوا: البعيد: الشهر فما فوقه، والقريب ما دون الشهر، وقيل: الشهر في مثل الدابة والمملوك قريب. (فتح) وللمشتري لو في الرؤية: أي إذا اختلف البائع والمشتري في الرؤية بأن قال البائع رأيته قبل البيع، وقال المشتري: ما رأيته قبل العقد، فالقول للمشتري بيمينه؛ لأنه أمر حادث والمشتري ينكره، فيكون القول قوله مع يمينه. رمز الحقائق: ۲۰/۲] عدلا أي عدل ثياب من القماش و لم يره وقبضه (ط) وهب وسلم: ثم اطلع على عيب في الباقي فهو بالخيار أمسكه إن شاء أو رده. (ط) رده بعيب: أي إذا اشترى عدل ثياب، فقبضه وتصرف في ثوب واحد من البيع أو الهبة مع التسليم، ثم وجد الباقي معيباً رده بسبب العيب، وليس البيع والهبة قيداً؛ لأن اللبس كذلك، ولا يمكنه أن يرد الباقي بخيار الرؤية والشرط سواء كان قبل القبض أو بعده؛ لما فيه من تفريق الصفقة قبل التمام، وفي خيار العيب يملك التفريق بعد القبض، فإن عاد إليه بسبب هو فسخ محض كالرد بخيار الرؤية أو الشرط أو العيب بقضاء أو الرجوع في الهبة، فهو على خيار الرؤية؛ لارتفاع المانع من الرد، وهو تفريق الصفقة، وعن أبي يوسف أن الخيار لا يعود؛ لأن الساقط لا يعود كخيار الشرط. (عيني، فتح) أو شرط لأن الرد قد تعذر بإخراج البعض عن ملكه. (فتح)
Chapter of Option of Seeing. From the book of Sales: And whoever buys what he saw has the option if it has changed, otherwise not. And if they dispute about the change, the statement is of the seller. The buyer does not have the option. The seller and buyer regarding the change: the just? And for the buyer regarding the seeing: And if he bought a bundle and sold from it a garment, or gifted and delivered, he returns it due to defect, not due to option of seeing or stipulation. They differed: He saw before the sale intending to purchase, knowing at the time of purchase that it is visible. (T, Ayni) He has option if it changed: meaning whoever bought something he saw before the purchase has the option if the thing changed from the description he saw it upon before that; because the contract occurred on an unknown description. Otherwise no: meaning if the thing did not change from the description he saw it upon, he has no option; because knowledge of the sold item was obtained by the first sight, and he was satisfied with it as long as it remains on that description. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 20/2] This is when at the time of seeing he intended to purchase, knowing that it is visible; if he saw it not intending to purchase then bought it, he has the option; similarly if he did not know at the time of purchase that it was visible, he also has the option due to lack of satisfaction; because satisfaction without knowledge of its attributes is inconceivable, and that sight did not inform him of the attributes of the sold item, so it is as if he did not see it. (Fath, Zayla'i) And if they dispute about the change: the buyer says it changed, the seller says it did not change, the statement is of the seller with oath, and the buyer bears the burden of proof; because the original principle is that what remains remains as it was, so the buyer is not believed in claiming change without his evidence, and the cause of bindingness—his prior sight—has appeared, and the apparent is a witness for the seller, so the statement is his. This is when the period is short, known that it does not change in such a period; if the period is long, such as he saw a young female slave then bought her after twenty years, and the seller claims she did not change, the statement is of the buyer. The period varies according to things: change of trees in a year, and animals in less due to lack of grazing. They said: remote is a month and above, near is less than a month; it is said: a month for animals and slaves is near. (Fath) And for the buyer regarding the seeing: if the seller and buyer dispute about the seeing, the seller says he saw it before the sale, the buyer says he did not see it before the contract, the statement is of the buyer with his oath; because it is an incident thing and the buyer denies it, so the statement is his with his oath. (T) He returns it due to defect: if he bought a bundle of cloth, took possession, and disposed of one garment by sale or gift with delivery, then found the rest defective, he returns it due to the defect. Sale and gift are not restrictions because wearing is similar. (Ayni, Fath) Or stipulation because the return has become impossible by removing some from his ownership. (Fath)

Commentary
This passage from Bab Khiyar al-Ru'yah explains the buyer's option when he has seen the item before purchase. The core ruling: if the item has changed from the state in which it was seen, the buyer has the option to rescind; if unchanged, the sale is binding. The author clarifies that this applies only if the buyer saw the item with the intention to purchase and was aware at the time of purchase that it was the same item he had seen. If he saw it without purchase intent, or did not know it was previously seen, the option exists because true satisfaction requires knowledge of attributes. When buyer and seller disagree on whether the item changed, the seller's word is taken with oath if the period is short; if long (e.g., twenty years), the buyer's word is taken. The definition of 'short' and 'long' varies: generally, less than a month is short, a month or more is long, but for animals and slaves a month may be considered short. If they dispute whether the buyer saw it at all, the buyer's word is taken because he denies a claim of prior sight. A sub-issue: if someone buys a bundle of cloth, uses one piece by sale or gift, then finds a defect in the rest, he may return the rest due to the defect — not due to khiyar al-ru'yah or khiyar al-shart — because using part splits the transaction. However, if the used piece is returned (e.g., by court judgment or revocation), the option of seeing is restored according to Abu Hanifa, because the obstacle is removed. Abu Yusuf holds it does not return, analogizing to khiyar al-shart.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): An option granted to a buyer who has seen the item before purchase to rescind the contract if the item has changed since inspection.
عدل (adl): A bundle of cloth or fabric sold as a set.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute about whether the item changed, when is the seller's word taken?
A) Always.
B) When the period since sight is short.
C) When the period since sight is long.
D) Never.

Key Takeaway
In disputes, the burden shifts based on time: seller's word for short periods, buyer's for long; and the bundle sub-issue shows the nuanced intra-Hanafi debate on the return of khiyar.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Buyer's Option Upon Finding a Defect: Khiyar al-'Ayb
Defines 'ayb and buyer's options for defective goods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of 'ayb, identify the conditions for khiyar al-'ayb, and apply the buyer's options of keeping or returning the defective item.

Core Idea
A defect gives the buyer the choice to keep with full price or return; price reduction is exceptional.

When you buy an item and later discover a defect, you might expect to get a discount. However, Hanafi law gives you a stark choice: accept it as is or return it. Only in very specific situations—like the seller causing the defect after sale—can you claim a proportional reduction. This lesson unpacks the definition of 'ayb, the conditions that trigger the option, and the reasoning behind the rule.

Guided Path
1
Define 'ayb
Identify the two types of defects (apparent and hidden) and the general principle that a defect is any deficiency that reduces market value among merchants.
2
List conditions for khiyar
Work through the four conditions: defect existed with seller, buyer unaware at sale and possession, no satisfaction after knowledge, no seller disclaimer.
All conditions must be met.
3
State the buyer’s options
The buyer may keep the item with full price or return it. He cannot force a discount unless the defect occurred by seller’s act after sale or another defect arises with the buyer.
Cost of return is on the buyer.
4
Examine the dalil
The proof is that soundness is implicitly required by the contract; when it is missing, the buyer has options just as if a stipulated description were missing. Cheating is prohibited by hadith.
The hadith: 'He who cheats us is not of us.'
5
Analyze examples and nuances
Review examples like ibaq (escape) and bed-wetting, and note the intra-Hanafi difference on whether escape from buyer to seller in the same village is a defect.
The better view is that it is a defect.

(ع) ف) وما أوجب نقصان الثمن: وإن لم تنقص العين ولا المنفعة كالظفر الأسود الصحيح القوي على العمل؛ لأن الضرر اللاحق بسبب العيب هو النقصان في المالية، فيرجع في معرفة النقصان إلى أهله وهم التجار وأرباب الصنائع، ولابد أن يكون العيب غير مختلف عندهم سواء أخبر الجميع بأنه عيب أو البعض فقط، ويكتفى بقول عدلين منهم رمز الحقائق: ٢١/٢] (فتح) عند التجار بضم التاء مع التشديد وبكسرها مع التخفيف جمع تاجر أو عند أرباب الصنائع إن كان المبيع من المصنوعات. (ف) كالإباق هو فرار العبد والجارية من المولى من غير ظلمه، فإن كان بظلمه سمي هروباً، فعلى هذا الإباق عيب والهرب ليس بعيب. (ف)] مطلقاً سواء كان الفرار من المولى أو ممن في يده بإجارة أو إعارة أو وديعة وإن كان فيما دون السفر، أما إذا غصبه ،رجل، فأبق منه إلى منزل ،مولاه فليس بعيب كما إذا أبق من المشتري إلى البائع و لم يختف عنده، وكانا في قرية واحدة في الثور، والأحسن أنه عيب. (فتح) والبول في الفراش لأن هذه الأفعال توجب نقصان القيمة عند التجار ، وهي عيوب في الصغير المميز. (ط، عيني)
Chapter of Option of Defect. i.e., explaining its rulings. Whoever finds in the sold item a defect takes it with full price or returns it. And what causes a decrease in the price is a defect among merchants, like running away and bed-wetting. Defect: i.e., it is a defect. That is, everything? The prices? Chapter of Option of Defect: an addition of something to its cause. It is a deficiency free from the original sound nature. It is of two types: apparent like blindness and water in the eye, and hidden like cough and cessation of menstruation for two months or more, and running away and similar. The intended meaning of defect: it was with the seller and the buyer did not see it at the sale or at possession, and no indication of satisfaction with it after knowledge of the defect appears from the buyer, and the seller did not stipulate immunity from it specifically or generally. (Miskin, Fath) He takes it with full price or returns it: meaning if he finds in the sold item a defect that decreases the price, and it was with the seller, and he took possession without knowing about it, and no indication of satisfaction with the defect appears from him, he is given a choice: if he wishes he takes the defective sold item with full price or returns it to the seller; because soundness is required by the absolute contract, so soundness is as if explicitly stipulated in the contract. So when it is lost, he has the option just as in the loss of a desired description stipulated in the contract. He does not deduct anything from the price because descriptions are not compensated by anything, except when the descriptions become intended by destruction, such as if the defect occurred by the seller's act after sale but before possession, where a proportional amount is deducted from the price if he chooses to take it, or if another defect occurs with the buyer where he has recourse for the decrease due to the defect on the seller as will come. Because soundness is as if stipulated, it is not permissible to conceal the defect in a sale or price, because cheating is forbidden. Ali said: 'He who cheats us is not of us.' [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 20/2] (Fath) Or returns it to the seller, and the cost of return is on the buyer. (Ayni, Fath) And what obligates a decrease in the price: even if the essence and benefit are not diminished, like a black nail that is sound and strong for work; because the harm due to the defect is the decrease in monetary value. So reference in knowing the decrease is to its people, namely the merchants and artisans. The defect must not be disputed among them; whether all inform that it is a defect or only some, and the statement of two just among them is sufficient. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 21/2] (Fath) Among merchants (with tashdid damma and takhfif kasra, plural of tajir) or among artisans if the sold item is from manufactured goods. (F) Like ibaq: it is the escape of a slave or slave girl from the master without oppression; if due to oppression, it is called huroob (flight). Accordingly, ibaq is a defect and huroob is not a defect. (F) Absolutely, whether the escape is from the master or from the one in whose possession he is by lease, loan, or deposit, even if within a short journey. But if a man usurps him and he escapes from him to his master's house, it is not a defect, just as if he escapes from the buyer to the seller and does not hide with him, and they are in one village, in al-Thawr, and the better view is that it is a defect. (Fath) And bed-wetting because these actions cause a decrease in value among merchants, and they are defects in a discerning minor. (T, Ayni)
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage from Bab Khiyar al-'Ayb defines the concept of defect ('ayb) in sales and states the buyer's options. A defect is any deficiency not present in a normally sound item, of two types: apparent (e.g., blindness) and hidden (e.g., cough, amenorrhea for two+ months, running away). For the buyer to have the option, the defect must have existed with the seller, the buyer must have been unaware at time of sale and possession, there must be no indication of satisfaction after knowledge, and the seller must not have disclaimed defects. Upon finding such a defect, the buyer may either accept the item with full price (no refund) or return it to the seller. The cost of return is on the buyer. He cannot demand a price reduction unless the defect occurred after sale but before possession due to the seller's act, in which case he may deduct proportionally; or if another defect arises with the buyer, he may claim the decrease from the seller. Concealing a defect is forbidden because it is cheating, as per the hadith. What constitutes a defect is determined by merchants or artisans; even a black nail that does not affect function is a defect if it reduces market value. Two just experts suffice. Examples are given: ibaq (running away from master without oppression) is a defect; if due to oppression it is huroob (flight) and not a defect. Ibaq includes escape from a lessee, borrower, or depositary, even for short distances. But if a usurper takes the slave and the slave escapes back to the master, it is not a defect. Similarly, escape from buyer to seller without hiding in the same village is debated; the better view is it is a defect. Bed-wetting is a defect in a discerning minor because it reduces value.

Key Terms
عيب (‘ayb): A deficiency that departs from the original sound nature, reducing value in the estimation of merchants; either apparent (like blindness) or hidden (like cough).
إباق (ibāq): The escape of a slave from their master without oppression; considered a defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when a buyer finds a defect in the purchased item, what is the default option?
A) Demand a proportional reduction in price.
B) Keep the item with full price or return it.
C) Keep the item and claim compensation from the seller.
D) Only return the item, not keep it.

Key Takeaway
A defect gives the buyer the choice to keep or return, not to demand a price reduction, unless the seller caused the defect after the sale.
